    Apple-Intelligence / Siri Glow — Flowing Edge Light

    Start here — the plain idea

    This is the colorful light that runs around the border of the screen when Siri or Apple Intelligence is listening — the modern replacement for the old Siri orb. Like the other glow effects, it's drawn entirely with math, no images.

    The recipe is just three moves. First, a mask: each pixel measures how far it is from the nearest screen edge, and only pixels near the border get to glow (bright at the edge, fading to nothing toward the center). Second, color that travels: instead of a fixed hue, the color sweeps around the perimeter over time, with a couple of overlapping waves layered in so it shimmers and never looks mechanical. Third, bloom: paint that color onto black and let overlapping light add up, so it reads as soft luminous glow.

    Once you notice the pattern — distance mask + flowing color + additive bloom — you've basically got the whole family of Apple glow effects. Move the mask to the bottom edge and it's the ambient light from the previous lesson; wrap it around the border and it's this.

    When Siri / Apple Intelligence is listening, a soft multi-colour light flows around the edges of the screen. It's the spiritual successor to the old Siri orb. The math is surprisingly approachable — a screen-edge mask, a hue that flows around the perimeter over time, and additive bloom. (Apple's exact version is private; this is how you recreate the feel.)

    The three ingredients

    1. Mask   → distance to the nearest screen edge → a glow that hugs the border
2. Colour → a hue that flows around the perimeter, animated over time + a little noise
3. Bloom  → add it onto black so overlapping light brightens (additive)

    1. The edge mask

    The glow lives near the border, so the key quantity is how far each pixel is from the nearest edge. In normalized uv (0–1), that's just:

    float edgeDist = min(min(uv.x, 1.0 - uv.x), min(uv.y, 1.0 - uv.y));
float glow = exp(-edgeDist / thickness);     // 1 at the edge, fading inward

    exp(-d/thickness) is the same exponential falloff as the ambient light and shaping functions — bright at the border, smoothly gone by the center. (For real screens you'd build this from a rounded-rect SDF, like Liquid Glass, so the glow rounds the corners.)

    2. Colour that flows around the edge

    The signature move is colour traveling around the perimeter. Parameterize position around the border by the angle from center, then make the hue a function of that angle plus time:

    float ang = atan2(uv.y - 0.5, uv.x - 0.5) / (2.0 * M_PI_F) + 0.5;   // 0..1 around
float flow = 0.12 * sin(ang * 18.0 + time * 1.3)
           + 0.08 * sin(ang * 7.0  - time * 0.8);                    // summed sines = shimmer
float hue = fract(ang + time * speed + flow);
half3 color = hsv2rgb(half3(hue, 0.85, 1.0));

    The ang + time*speed term sweeps the rainbow around the edge; the summed sines (incommensurate frequencies, 15-noise-and-patterns) add the living, non-mechanical shimmer — exactly the "gently alive, never looping" trick from your interaction-math oscillation & noise notes. Apple's real version reads more like a mesh gradient (a few moving colour anchors) than a pure hue sweep, but the principle — a small set of flowing colours mapped around the border — is the same.

    3. Bloom (additive)

    Output the colour multiplied by the glow mask onto black, so where light overlaps it adds and brightens — additive blending (16-blending-and-compositing):

    return half4(color * glow, glow);            // premultiplied; add over dark UI

    A second, wider, dimmer pass (larger thickness, lower intensity) gives the soft outer halo that real bloom has.

    Putting it together

    It's a full-screen layerEffect (or an overlay view) behind/around your content, driven by TimelineView(.animation) for time — same delivery as Metal in SwiftUI and animation in shaders. Fade the whole thing in/out with a progress uniform when Siri starts/stops, just like the ambient light's reveal.

    Try it

    The demo above is this recipe: edge-distance mask × flowing hue × bloom, with thickness, flow-speed, and intensity sliders. Crank the speed and watch the colour chase around the border.

    Why it's a great study piece

    It's the same three-part pattern as the ambient light (mask → flowing colour → bloom), just shaped to the screen border instead of the bottom. Once you see that "Apple glow effects = a distance mask + flowing colour + additive bloom," you can build the family — listening states, focus rings, notification reveals — from one mental template.

    The foundation

    • edge mask = each pixel's distance to the nearest screen edge, turned into "how much glow lives here" — bright at the border, gone by the center.
    • exponential falloff (exp(-d/thickness)) = the smooth fade from the edge inward; bigger thickness = a wider glow band.
    • flowing hue = mapping color to angle-around-the-border plus time, so the rainbow sweeps around the perimeter.
    • summed sines = a couple of overlapping waves at different frequencies added in, giving living shimmer that never visibly loops.
    • additive bloom = painting color onto black so overlapping light adds and brightens, the way real glow stacks.
    • progress uniform = a Swift-driven value to fade the whole effect in/out when Siri starts and stops listening.
